The model (`docs/specs/window-views.md`, rules R1–R7): **a window ROW is a substrate** (a supervised tmux pane); **a VIEW is a lens** over one derivable output of that pane (the tty is a lens; an iframe of the pane's HTTP service is a lens; the parsed agent transcript is a lens; later: desktop). **Which lenses a window offers is a derived capability set; which lens YOU look through is per-viewer client state** carried in the URL + localStorage — never a server-side `@rk_type` mutation, never part of the window's identity. `260714-t97o-web-view-lens` built the generalized switcher machinery (spec R4 — "whichever ships first builds it") and retrofitted the shipped iframe feature onto it; **the chat view (`260714-r7rq`) folds into this SAME machinery** (its interim `?view=chat`-only mechanism — `chat-view-resolve.ts`, `use-chat-view-pref.ts`, `SegmentedViewToggle` — was retired). Frontend-only; no Go/API changes (`@rk_type`/`@rk_url`/`@rk_chat` plumbing and `POST /options` are untouched — the SSE payload already carried `rkType`/`rkUrl`/`chatProvider`).

Three lenses are implemented: `tty` (always available, `TerminalClient`), `web` (available when `rkUrl` is non-empty, `IframeWindow`), and `chat` (available when `chatProvider` is non-empty, `ChatView` — the read-only transcript renderer, § Chat View). Capabilities are orthogonal and STACK (spec R5): one window can offer `tty`+`web`+`chat` at once. The registry is open-ended — `desktop` adds a `ViewName` member, an availability clause, a `defaultView` hint, and a `ViewSwitcher` segment, NOT a new component/route/window-type.

### Pure view-model helper — `lib/window-view.ts`

The single source of view logic — pure, DOM-free, colocated `window-view.test.ts` (the same pattern as `window-transition.ts`/`navigation.ts`). Both the `app.tsx` render branch AND the window-switch transition classification (§ Window-Switch Slide Transition) call `resolveView`, so it MUST live in one place (no drift). Helpers take a minimal structural `{ rkType?, rkUrl?, chatProvider? }` shape (assignable from `WindowInfo`):

- **`ViewName = "tty" | "web" | "chat"`** — the lens union.
- **`hasWebUrl(win)` / `hasChat(win)`** — the single-source availability predicates: `rkUrl` non-empty after `.trim()` (whitespace-only `@rk_url` is NOT web — no blank-src iframe); `chatProvider` non-empty (mirrors the backend `resolveWindowChat` gate).
- **`availableViews(win): ViewName[]`** (spec R1/R3) — `["tty"]`, plus `"web"` when `hasWebUrl`, plus `"chat"` when `hasChat`. **Availability is decoupled from `@rk_type`**: an iframe-typed window with no URL offers only `tty` (matches the old render gate's AND-condition). Returned in the registry's fixed order (`chat > web > tty`) via a `HINT_ORDER` filter — so a stacked window yields `["chat","web","tty"]`.
- **`defaultView(win): ViewName`** (spec R5) — the window's default lens, applied ONLY when the URL and localStorage carry no choice: `"web"` when `rkType === "iframe"` AND `rkUrl` is set, else `"tty"`. `@rk_type=iframe` is **demoted from identity to a creation-time default-view hint** (no data migration). Structured as spec R5's ordered hint precedence `desktop > chat > web > tty` (module const `HINT_ORDER`, only `web`/`tty` wired) so later lenses add a hint clause, not a branch. **`chat` sits in `HINT_ORDER` for capability ORDERING only — it contributes NO default hint**: a chat-capable window still defaults to `tty` unless the viewer chose chat (preserves `260714-r7rq`'s terminal-default; a chat-capable window opens on the terminal, chat is one click / `Ctrl+\`` away).
- **`resolveView(searchView, stored, win): ViewName`** (spec R2) — precedence **URL `?view=` (if that view is available) → localStorage (if available) → `defaultView(win)`**. Any unavailable value falls through; the chain always bottoms out at `tty`, so an unavailable `?view=web` deep link (window with no `rkUrl`) OR `?view=chat` on a chat-less window renders the terminal, never a broken iframe / empty chat shell. `searchView`/`stored` are untrusted strings validated against the capability set here — callers pass raw values.
- **`nextView(available, current): ViewName | null`** — the cycle successor (wraps); `null` when < 2 views or `current` is absent. Powers the `Cmd/Ctrl+.` chord (pure so the order is unit-testable).
- **`shouldSuppressViewChord(target): boolean`** — the input-gating predicate for the chord, **byte-for-byte the same rule as `shell.tsx`'s `⌘\` sidebar toggle**: suppress only inside a NON-xterm INPUT/TEXTAREA/contenteditable (xterm's hidden helper textarea is the terminal's normal focus, so it must NOT be suppressed — `target.closest(".xterm") != null` is the exception). jsdom-safe (`contentEditable` attribute fallback for the missing `isContentEditable` getter).
- **localStorage helpers** — **value-bearing** key `runkit-window-view:{server}:{windowId}` storing the view NAME, now including `"chat"` (absent = default). `windowViewStorageKey`/`readStoredView`/`writeStoredView`, try/catch-noop per `chrome-context.tsx`. **This supersedes the chat plan's key-present `runkit:chat-view:` `board-autofit`-style convention** (spec R2 explicitly supersedes; no data migration — the interim keys were live only hours and self-correct on the next toggle) — value-bearing generalizes past two states.

### `?view=` search param — `router.tsx`

`view` is a **validated search param** on `terminalRoute` (spec R2, Constitution IV: no new route — it is the codebase's first `validateSearch`). The exported pure `validateTerminalSearch(search): { view?: "web" | "chat" }` accepts `view === "web"` or `view === "chat"` and **drops any other/unknown/non-string value** (returns `{}` — treated as absent, NEVER errored), so a stale/garbage deep link degrades to the default view. It is wired as the route's `validateSearch` (ONE key — the merge briefly had two) and unit-tested directly in `router.test.ts` (accepts `web`/`chat`, drops `?view=bogus`/non-string/absent without throwing). The `declare module "@tanstack/react-router"` `Register` block types `.view` as `"web" | "chat" | undefined`, so `useSearch({ strict: false })` in `app.tsx` reads it **with no `as` cast** (code-quality type-narrowing — `tsc --noEmit` clean).

### `app.tsx` integration — resolution, `switchView`, render branch

`app.tsx` (terminal route) computes `searchView = useSearch({ strict: false }).view`, `storedView = readStoredView(server, windowParam)`, `currentViews = availableViews(currentWindow)` (memoized), and `resolvedView = resolveView(searchView, storedView, currentWindow)`. There is ONE view-state block (the chat feature's parallel `resolveChatView`/`useChatViewPref`/`activeView` block was deleted). It owns one stable `switchView(view)` callback (deps `server`/`windowParam`/`navigate`):
- writes localStorage (`writeStoredView`),
- `navigate({ to: "/$server/$window", params, search: view !== "tty" ? { view } : {}, replace: true })` — **`web`/`chat` ride the URL (`?view=web` / `?view=chat`); `tty` DROPS the param** (clean URL; tty is the always-available default). The URL is the shareable/deep-linkable seam (push-notification-ready); localStorage is the per-window stickiness that survives R6's param-drop on a window switch. Both seams are required.

The **render branch** selects the renderer by resolved view — `chatViewActive ? <ChatView …/> : resolvedView === "web" && currentWindow?.rkUrl ? <IframeWindow onSwitchToTty={() => switchView("tty")} …/> : <TerminalClient/>`, where `chatViewActive = resolvedView === "chat"` (`resolveView` already bakes in the `chatProvider` availability gate, so a chat-less window never resolves to chat — no separate `chatAvailable` guard). NOT by `rkType === "iframe" && rkUrl`. The **tty-branch "Switch to iframe view" `</>` hint bar** (a SECOND `@rk_type`-mutation site that called `updateWindowType(..., "iframe")`) is **removed** — switching to web is now the ViewSwitcher/palette/`>_` job, none of which mutate `@rk_type` (spec R7).

### ViewSwitcher chip — `components/view-switcher.tsx`

The ONE switcher UX all lenses share (spec R4) — a generic segmented chip: props `{ views: ViewName[]; active: ViewName; onSelect }`. Mounted in the top-bar **L1 tier** (terminal cluster, leading SplitButton/FixedWidthToggle), fed via the `useRegisterTopBarSlot` slot context (`availableViews`/`activeView`/`onSelectView` are the ONLY view fields on the slot — the chat feature's `view`/`chatAvailable`/`onSetView` were removed). Renders `null` when `views.length <= 1` (both the chip and the caller gate on this, so a tty-only window shows no chip). Presentational — owns no view logic.

- **Segment DISPLAY order is `[tty|web|chat]`** via a component-local `DISPLAY_ORDER = ["tty","web","chat"]`, **deliberately decoupled from `window-view.ts`'s `HINT_ORDER`** (`chat>web>tty`, which governs only default/capability precedence — the two orderings answer different questions). Any view not in `DISPLAY_ORDER` sorts to the END (defensive — a future lens still renders); later lenses slot into `DISPLAY_ORDER`.
- Active segment is **inverse-video** (`bg-accent-green text-bg-primary`); house `rk-glint` hover vocabulary (reduced-motion-safe — the glint is a CSS media-query no-op, no JS animation). `role="group"` + `data-testid="view-toggle"` + per-segment `aria-pressed`/`aria-label` (`Terminal view`/`Web view`/`Chat view`). **Visible at ALL breakpoints** (`inline-flex`, NO `hidden sm:*` gate — unlike its L1 siblings) because chat/web are primary mobile use cases (the 80-col tmux minimum is run-kit's worst mobile ergonomic). Segment glyphs are the **lowercase view names** `tty`/`web`/`chat` (spec R4's `[tty|chat]` style).

### Palette parity + keyboard shortcuts (Constitution V)

- **`View: Terminal` / `View: Web` / `View: Chat` palette actions** (AppShell `viewActions` in `app.tsx`), each visible only when its view is **available AND not the current** view — the gating + label + shortcut-hint composition live in a pure builder `buildViewActions(available, resolved, onSwitch)` in `lib/palette-view.ts` (mirrors `lib/palette-move.ts`/`palette-update.ts`, unit-tested in `palette-view.test.ts`). The per-entry `shortcut` hint tracks the binding that reaches it: `View: Chat` (and `View: Terminal` when LEAVING chat) show `` Ctrl+` `` (the chat toggle); every other switch shows `⌘.` (the cycle). These **REPLACE the retired `toggle-iframe-terminal` action** (which mutated `@rk_type`) AND the chat feature's second `buildViewActions(chatAvailable, activeView, onSetView)` call (one call now).
- **`Cmd/Ctrl+.` cycles the current window's lenses** — a window-level `keydown` effect in `app.tsx` that `preventDefault()`s (so xterm doesn't also receive it), gated by `shouldSuppressViewChord` and calling `switchView(nextView(views, active))`. No-op when < 2 views. Live view/window values read via a `viewCycleRef` so the listener is stable across SSE ticks. Chosen against the live chord registry (`⌘K` palette, `⌘\` sidebar, `⌘]`/`⌘[` board pane-cycle) — a free binding in the `⌘<punctuation>` family; `Ctrl+.` is inert in readline (unlike `Ctrl+/`→undo). Documented in the **App section of the Keyboard Shortcuts dialog** (`ShortcutRow label="Cycle view" keys={["⌘."]}`).
- **`` Ctrl+` `` toggles tty↔chat** (`use-chat-view-shortcut.ts`, § Chat View → shortcut) — the shipped VS-Code "toggle terminal" binding, now speaking `ViewName` (`"tty"`, not `"terminal"`), enabled when `currentViews.includes("chat")`, toggling via `switchView`. Documented as `ShortcutRow label="Toggle chat / terminal" keys={["Ctrl+\`"]}`.

### Heading is a static `Window:` in every lens (spec R4 reversal — `260714-uco1`)

The top-bar center `PageType: name` heading on the terminal route reads a **static `Window: <window>` in every lens** (tty / web / chat) — it does NOT follow the active view (§ Window Heading). A single `WINDOW_PREFIX = "Window:"` constant (`top-bar.tsx`) replaces the retired `TERMINAL_PREFIX` and is passed as a constant `prefix` into `WindowHeading` at the terminal-mode center cell; the lens-following `terminalHeadingPrefix()` helper and the `WEB_PREFIX`/`CHAT_PREFIX` constants were **removed**. Rationale (`260714-uco1`, a deliberate reversal of `docs/specs/window-views.md` R4's "the center page heading follows the lens" sentence — updated in-spec within that change): the heading identifies the WINDOW (the substrate); which lens you look through is shown by the L1 `ViewSwitcher`, not the heading (per window-views.md "rows are substrates, views are lenses"). Bonus: the name's anchor no longer jumps on a lens switch, since the prefix width no longer changes with the lens (§ Center-heading stable anchor + nav affordances). The click-to-rename affordance and boot-sweep treatment are unchanged. (The `WindowHeading` prefix-flip replay machinery — `prevPrefixRef` + the prefix-keyed effect, `top-bar.tsx` ~:1053/:1108 — is now inert since the sole call site passes the constant `WINDOW_PREFIX`; it survives as a plan-recorded deletion candidate.)

### `?view` drops on window switch (spec R6)

Navigating to a DIFFERENT window carries NO `view` param — each destination window resolves its own last-view/default independently. Client-side navigations (sidebar/palette/breadcrumb via `navigateToWindow`, plus the window-death redirect and SSE-writeback switch) omit/clear `search`, and TanStack Router's `final` search middleware returns `{}` when `dest.search` is absent, so an outgoing `?view=web`/`?view=chat` does not leak onto the target. (Simplest semantics — per-window localStorage covers the intent; the web-view-lens e2e persistence case exercises this through a real sidebar-click navigation to guard against a future `retainSearchParams`/router-upgrade regression.) The one exception is the `Agent: Next waiting` / WaitingBadge deep-link, which INTENTIONALLY sets `?view=chat` for a chat-capable target (§ Chat View → WaitingBadge).

### Window-switch transition classification (one rule)

The window-switch slide transition's `switchTransitionRef` carries a SINGLE `ungatedIds` set: window ids whose EFFECTIVE resolved view is **not `tty`** — i.e. they render `<IframeWindow>` (web) or `<ChatView>` (chat), neither of which has the terminal's xterm first-write receipt seam, so they must use the transition's **ungated capture** (a first-write gate would never release for a non-xterm surface → stuck transition / blank pane). Computed at render time from `resolveView(undefined, readStoredView(server, id), win) !== "tty"` (URL is unknown for a not-yet-navigated target, so only localStorage + default hint decide). This replaced the merge's TWO sets (`iframeIds` via `=== "web"` + a lazy-`readChatViewPrefKey` `chatCapableIds`) with one `resolveView`-keyed classification — the same "keyed on resolveView, not `@rk_type`" invariant as the render branch (§ Window-Switch Slide Transition).

### e2e — `web-view-lens.spec.ts` / `chat-view.spec.ts` (+ `.spec.md`)

`web-view-lens.spec.ts` drives real tmux (own session, `window-heading.spec.ts` pattern), setting `@rk_url`/`@rk_type` via `tmux set-option -w`. Covers, at 375px + desktop: chip appears only on web-capable windows; flip to web then back preserves the window and fires **zero `/options` POSTs** (asserted via `page.on("request")`); deep link `?view=web` cold-loads the iframe (lens proven by the web chip / iframe + the `?view=web` URL — the heading stays the static `Window:` prefix since `260714-uco1`, no longer a lens indicator); `?view=web` on a URL-less window falls back to the terminal; legacy `@rk_type=iframe`+url defaults to web with the chip present; last-view persistence across a real client-side window switch away and back; the switcher chip is **visible at 375px** (all breakpoints). `chat-view.spec.ts` (fully mocked SSE + chat stream) covers the chat lens through the SAME unified chip (`view-toggle`, `Chat view` segment): chip gated on `chatProvider`, flip to chat (lens proven via `view-toggle`/`chat-view` presence + `?view=chat` URL, not the heading prefix), the `` Ctrl+` `` toggle, `?view=chat` cold-load, the bubble/tool-card/pending renderer, mobile budget, reduced-motion.

## Chat View (`260714-r7rq-chat-read-frontend`)

A **read-only HTML chat view over the SAME agent pane** — a second view over the tmux pane, never a substrate (the pane stays the agent's parent, Constitution VI; the view only renders the streamed transcript). It is the **`chat` lens** of the window-view model (§ Window Views (Lens Model)) — addressed by `?view=chat` on the existing `/$server/$window` terminal route (Constitution IV, no new route). **All view-state plumbing — the `?view=` param, availability gate, the ViewSwitcher chip, localStorage persistence, palette parity, the `` Ctrl+` `` shortcut, and the switch-transition classification — is the UNIFIED machinery** described in § Window Views (Lens Model); this section owns only what is chat-SPECIFIC: the `chatProvider` gate, the connection-dot semantics, the renderer/stream, and the WaitingBadge deep-link. (The heading is no longer part of the plumbing — since `260714-uco1` it reads a static `Window:` in every lens, § Heading is a static `Window:`.) The renderer + data layer live in `architecture.md`/[chat](/run-kit/chat.md) § Chat View Frontend. Change 3 of the HTML-agent-chat-view stack (consumes the Change-2 backend, `chat.md`).

**The `chatProvider` gate.** `WindowInfo` gained `chatProvider?: string` + `chatSessionRef?: string` (`types.ts`) — the window-level `@rk_chat` rollup the backend already emitted (typed, not newly parsed). **A non-empty `chatProvider` is the SOLE availability gate** for the chat lens (`hasChat(win)` in `window-view.ts`) — mirroring the backend's own `resolveWindowChat` gating — so it transitively gates every chat affordance: the ViewSwitcher chat segment, the `View: Chat` palette action, the `` Ctrl+` `` shortcut (enabled iff `currentViews.includes("chat")`), the `<ChatView>` renderer, and the deep-link append. (The heading is NOT among them — since `260714-uco1` it is a static `Window:` in every lens, § Heading is a static `Window:`.) There is NO separate `chatAvailable` variable anymore — `resolveView`/`availableViews` fold the gate in.

### View state = the unified lens machinery (NOT a chat-specific mechanism)

The interim chat-only mechanism was **retired** and folded into the lens machinery:
- `lib/chat-view-resolve.ts` (`resolveChatView`, the chat-only `validateTerminalSearch`) — **DELETED**. Resolution is `resolveView` (URL→localStorage→default); `router.tsx`'s single `validateTerminalSearch` accepts `web`|`chat` (§ Window Views → `?view=`).
- `hooks/use-chat-view-pref.ts` (the `runkit:chat-view:` key-presence pref + `readChatViewPrefKey`) — **DELETED**. Persistence is the value-bearing `runkit-window-view:` key (which now also stores `"chat"`); no migration.
- `SegmentedViewToggle` in `top-bar.tsx` + its `view`/`chatAvailable`/`onSetView` slot fields + `onSetView` toggle body — **DELETED**. The chip is the generic `ViewSwitcher` (`[tty|chat]` segments for a chat-only-capable window); flipping is `switchView("chat")`/`switchView("tty")`.
- `chatViewActive = resolvedView === "chat"` is the render + stream gate (`resolveView` already gated on `chatProvider`).

### Center heading `Window: <window>` (static in the chat lens too)

The `chat` lens does NOT change the heading prefix — since `260714-uco1` the top-bar heading is a static `Window: <window>` in every lens (§ Heading is a static `Window:`; § Window Heading for the boot-sweep/rename mechanics). The `<ChatView>` renderer preserves the inline-rename affordance (the heading IS the rename surface, especially on mobile) — the same parametrized `WindowHeading`, no fork.

### Renderer swap + chat stream (`app.tsx`)

In the `windowParam` render arm, `chatViewActive` selects `<ChatView>` AHEAD of the web-vs-terminal branch (`chatViewActive ? <ChatView> : resolvedView === "web" && rkUrl ? <IframeWindow> : <TerminalClient>`). `AppShell` owns the single `useChatStream(server, windowId)` call (opened only when `chatViewActive`, else passed empty strings so the hook idles) and passes `{events, pending, connected, error}` into `ChatView` — ONE `EventSource` feeds both the renderer and the connection dot (below). The chat pane joins the switch-transition **ungated capture** through the unified `ungatedIds` classification (any non-`tty` resolved view; § Window Views → Window-switch transition classification) — `<ChatView>` has NO xterm first-write seam, so a first-write gate would never release.

### Connection dot = chat stream health in chat mode (R9)

"Dot-everywhere = per-page live-data health" (§ Chrome (Top Bar) → connection dot). In chat view, the `isConnected` `AppShell` registers into `TopBarSlot` reflects the **chat stream's** health instead of the per-server sessions-SSE slice: `dotConnected = chatViewActive ? chatStream.connected : isConnected` (`chatStream.connected` is the 3s-debounced health from `use-chat-stream`). In terminal/web view the value is unchanged.

### WaitingBadge click + `Agent: Next waiting` deep-link into `?view=chat`

`WaitingBadge` (`components/waiting-badge.tsx`) gained an **optional** `onClick` prop: when passed, the badge renders as a `<button>` (rk-glint hover, `stopPropagation` so it doesn't bubble to the parent row) that navigates to the next waiting window in its scope; when absent, it keeps today's **display-only** `<span>` (so the board-header / Cockpit-tile / server-panel mount sites, which pass no onClick, are unchanged). It is currently wired ONLY at the **sidebar session row** (`session-row.tsx` → `sidebar/index.tsx` → `AppShell`'s `handleWaitingBadgeClick`) — the one surface with a navigable per-session scope.

`handleWaitingBadgeClick(srv, sess)` (`app.tsx`) builds the clicked session's ordered waiting windows and calls **`nextWaitingTarget(ordered, server, windowParam)`** (`lib/palette-agent-nav.ts` — REUSED, not re-implemented; the R12/A-024 review-rework fix: the first cut picked the session's FIRST waiting window via `windows.find(isWaiting)`, so clicking the badge while already ON its first waiting window was a no-op instead of advancing to the next). It appends `?view=chat` via the pure `chatSearchForTarget(hasChat)` helper (`lib/palette-agent-nav.ts`, unit-tested) — `{ view: "chat" }` iff the target window has a `chatProvider`, else empty search (the target resolves its own pref). This is the ONE intentional `?view=` carry across a window switch (§ Window Views → `?view` drops). The existing `Agent: Next waiting` palette action gets the **same** `chatSearchForTarget` append rule for any target it navigates to.

### Connection dot = chat stream health in chat mode (R9)

"Dot-everywhere = per-page live-data health" (§ Chrome (Top Bar) → connection dot). In chat view, the `isConnected` `AppShell` registers into `TopBarSlot` reflects the **chat stream's** health instead of the per-server sessions-SSE slice: `dotConnected = chatViewActive ? chatStream.connected : isConnected` (`chatStream.connected` is the 3s-debounced health from `use-chat-stream`). In terminal/root view the value is unchanged.

### WaitingBadge click + `Agent: Next waiting` deep-link into `?view=chat`

`WaitingBadge` (`components/waiting-badge.tsx`) gained an **optional** `onClick` prop: when passed, the badge renders as a `<button>` (rk-glint hover, `stopPropagation` so it doesn't bubble to the parent row) that navigates to the next waiting window in its scope; when absent, it keeps today's **display-only** `<span>` (so the board-header / Cockpit-tile / server-panel mount sites, which pass no onClick, are unchanged). It is currently wired ONLY at the **sidebar session row** (`session-row.tsx` → `sidebar/index.tsx` → `AppShell`'s `handleWaitingBadgeClick`) — the one surface with a navigable per-session scope.

`handleWaitingBadgeClick(srv, sess)` (`app.tsx`) builds the clicked session's ordered waiting windows and calls **`nextWaitingTarget(ordered, server, windowParam)`** (`lib/palette-agent-nav.ts` — REUSED, not re-implemented; the R12/A-024 review-rework fix: the first cut picked the session's FIRST waiting window via `windows.find(isWaiting)`, so clicking the badge while already ON its first waiting window was a no-op instead of advancing to the next). It appends `?view=chat` via the pure `chatSearchForTarget(hasChat)` helper (`lib/palette-agent-nav.ts`, unit-tested) — `{ view: "chat" }` iff the target window has a `chatProvider`, else empty search (the target resolves its own pref). The existing `Agent: Next waiting` palette action gets the **same** `chatSearchForTarget` append rule for any target it navigates to.

## Boards View

`/board/$name` renders a horizontal pane dashboard for windows pinned to a named board (see `tmux-sessions.md` § Pin Sessions / § `@rk_board` for storage and `architecture.md` § Boards Feature for the route placement rationale). The board view does NOT mount AppShell, but it shares the same root-mounted multi-server `SessionProvider`, the same unified `<Sidebar>`, and as of `260509-17m3-rotated-shell-layout` the same `<Shell>` grid wrapper — the sidebar's per-server session groups stay populated across the route switch because the provider lives at the root.

### SESSIONS-vs-BOARDS exclusivity (a pinned window is physically MOVED)

Since `260602-qn62-move-based-board-pin-sessions`, pinning a window **physically moves** it (`tmux move-window`) out of its home session into its own single-window pin-session (`_rk-pin-<id>`), so a window is in **exactly one** view at a time — SESSIONS (its home session) or BOARDS (a pane on the board), never both. A pinned window therefore **disappears from its home session's window list in the SESSIONS sidebar** until it is unpinned (which moves it back to `@rk_home`, appending at the next index). This is intended and is what lets a board pane attach the relay DIRECTLY to the pin-session (no ephemeral). It is also "already true" for the sidebar with no frontend work: the SSE session snapshot no longer lists the moved window under its home session (pin-sessions are filtered at the `parseSessions` chokepoint), so the sidebar reflects it automatically. The pin-icon filled state and the active-board accent (below) are the only board-aware affordances on a SESSIONS row — and a pinned window's row is simply absent from its home group while pinned.

### BoardPage Layout (`app/frontend/src/components/board/board-page.tsx`)

BoardPage uses the shared `<Shell>` wrapper. Since `260707-4vq2-lift-topbar-root-layout` the Shell grid carries NO `topbar` row — the desktop grid is `grid-template-areas: "sidebar content" / "sidebar bottombar"` (rows `1fr auto`; collapses to single-column `"content" "bottombar"` on `< 640px` with the sidebar overlay); the TopBar is mounted once at the persistent root layout above the Shell, not as a grid child (see § Shell Grid Layout / § Chrome (Top Bar) → persistent root mount). Children are placed into named grid areas:

- **Sidebar** (`gridArea: "sidebar"`) — the unified `<Sidebar currentServer={null}>` (same component as AppShell). No per-server group is marked current on board routes. Per-server session groups + Boards section + ServerPanel + bottom panels render as on AppShell. Mobile (`< 640px`) renders the sidebar as a Shell-level overlay whose grid child spans `gridRow: "1 / 3"` (content + bottombar, re-indexed by `4vq2` from `"2 / 4"` now that the topbar row is gone) — same overlay implementation as AppShell
- **TopBar** — NO LONGER a Shell grid child (`4vq2`). `BoardPageContent` deleted its `<header style={{ gridArea: "topbar" }}><TopBar mode="board" …/></header>` block + `TopBar` import (keeping `HELP_URL` for its palette action) and instead registers the board extras (`boardName: name`, `paneCount: entries.length`, `serverCount`, `waitingPaneCount`, `boards`, `onCloseFocused: unpinFocused`, `closeDisabled: entries.length === 0`, `isConnected: boardConnected`, `sidebarOpen`, `onToggleSidebar`) into the slot context via `useRegisterTopBarSlot`. The persistent `RootTopBar` derives `mode="board"` + `boardName` from the route and renders the board bar fed by those extras (breadcrumb/heading/right-cluster content unchanged from before the move — see § Board and § center cell for the current board rendering, which supersedes the retired `Board ▸ {name} ▾` breadcrumb and the board-hides-dot behavior)
- **Content** (`gridArea: "content"`) — the existing `DesktopRow` (desktop) / `MobileCarousel` (mobile) horizontally-scrollable container of pane "cards" sorted by `orderKey`. Each card is a `BoardPane` with a `BoardHeader` (`<window-name> · <server>` + unpin button) and an embedded `TerminalClient` connected via WebSocket to `/relay/{windowId}?server=<entry.server>` (one WS per pane) — **the same `TerminalClient`/relay path as the normal terminal route**. Since `260602-qn62` the `windowId` resolves to the window's `_rk-pin-*` pin-session server-side (the relay attaches directly to it), so `BoardPane`/`board-page.tsx` need NO structural change — the move is transparent to the component (`BoardEntry` shape unchanged). The horizontal-scroll viewport begins at the `content` grid area's left edge — flush with `sidebar.right` (or page.left when `sidebarOpen === false`); no left gutter for board-level chrome
- **BottomBar** (`gridArea: "bottombar"`) — the shared `<BottomBar>` (NEW on this route — board route had no BottomBar pre-rotation). Byte-identical to AppShell's invocation: same three callbacks (`onOpenCompose`, `onFocusTerminal`, `onScrollLockChange`). `onOpenCompose` calls `setComposeOpen(true)` from `FocusedTerminalContext`; `onFocusTerminal` invokes a ref-tracked `focusFocusedPaneRef.current()` that re-focuses the currently-focused board pane via its `paneRefs[focusedIndex].focus()`; `onScrollLockChange` plumbs through `DesktopRow`/`MobileCarousel` → `BoardPane` → `TerminalClient.scrollLocked`. Input target is the focused pane's wsRef (read from `FocusedTerminalContext.focused?.wsRef`)
- **Own `<CommandPalette>` mount** — BoardPage retains its own palette mount because board-route-only entries (Switch / Leave Board View / Cycle Pane Focus →/←) need a registration site, and the AppShell palette doesn't mount on `/board/<name>`. The mount is preserved through the rotation

Empty / non-existent board (`name` exists in URL but `getBoard` returns `[]`): shows "No panes pinned to this board yet. Pin a window from the sidebar." with a back link.

### Pane Cards (Desktop)

- **Default width 480px**, drag-resizable between 280px (min) and viewport-minus-sidebar (max). Resize handle hidden on coarse-pointer devices
- **Persisted per-board** in `localStorage["runkit:board-widths:<name>"]` as `Record<windowId, number>`. `usePaneWidths(boardName)` encapsulates read/write/clamp; missing entries fall back to 480px; malformed JSON is ignored silently. Pane widths are intentionally browser-local view state — they do NOT cross devices (pin state in tmux does)
- **Click-to-focus** transfers focus to the pane's xterm via a `useImperativeHandle`-exposed `focus()` method on `BoardPaneHandle`. **Hover-to-focus is OFF in v1** (no hover handler attached)
- **Visual focus indicator** — focused pane has a distinct border/glow; unfocused panes are de-emphasized
- **Keyboard pane cycling** — `Cmd+]` / `Ctrl+]` next (wraps), `Cmd+[` / `Ctrl+[` previous (wraps). Bound via a `useEffect` keydown listener on the BoardPage component
- **Autofit override** — when the per-board autofit toggle is ON, desktop panes ignore the stored pixel width and become equal-share flex items, and the resize handle is hidden. See § Board Autofit Toggle. Autofit never mutates `runkit:board-widths:<name>`, so toggling off restores the exact hand-tuned widths above.

### Board Autofit Toggle (`260708-738w-board-autofit`)

A per-board **desktop** toggle that stretches panes to fill the row instead of using explicit pixel widths — the minimal-surface answer (Constitution IV: one button + one palette action, no settings page) to boards chronically under-using screen width with 2–3 panes on a wide monitor. Desktop `DesktopRow` only — the `MobileCarousel` is already one full-width `w-full` pane, so autofit is a **no-op on mobile** (no branch there).

**Persistence — `useBoardAutofit` (`app/frontend/src/hooks/use-board-autofit.ts`)**, mirroring the guard discipline of `use-pane-widths.ts`:

- Key `runkit:board-autofit:<board>` (exported prefix `BOARD_AUTOFIT_LOCALSTORAGE_PREFIX = "runkit:board-autofit:"`), **per-board** — enabling autofit on board A does not affect board B, and switching `board` reloads state via a `useEffect`-on-`board` (the same reload seam `usePaneWidths` uses).
- **"on" sentinel with key removal on off**: the literal string `"on"` is the ONLY value that reads as on; anything else (absent, malformed) reads off (window-undefined bail + `try/catch`, malformed-tolerant like `use-pane-widths.ts`). Turning autofit OFF **removes the key** (`localStorage.removeItem`) rather than storing `"off"` — the read is `getItem(...) === "on"`, so there is no `"off"` state to persist.
- **Default off** (no key stored → current per-pane-width behavior); the key is untouched until the setter runs.
- API: `useBoardAutofit(board) → { autofit, toggleAutofit }`; `toggleAutofit` flips + persists and round-trips across a fresh hook instance / reload.

**Layout branch — `DesktopRow` / `BoardPane` (`board-page.tsx`, `board-pane.tsx`)**. `BoardPage` owns `useBoardAutofit(name)` and passes `autofit` down to `DesktopRow`, which forwards it to each `BoardPane` and passes `showResizeHandle={!autofit}`:

- **Autofit ON**: `DesktopRow` passes **no pixel `width`** (`width={autofit ? undefined : getWidth(entry.windowId)}`); each pane root becomes `flex: 1 1 0` with `min-width: max(BOARD_PANE_MIN_WIDTH, calc(25% - 3px))` (import the `BOARD_PANE_MIN_WIDTH` constant from `use-pane-widths` — 280px — never hard-code) inside the existing `overflow-x-auto flex gap-1 p-1` row. Classes drop `w-full`/`shrink-0`; the flex+min-width in `style` drives sizing. Result: ≤4 panes stretch to share the row equally with no horizontal scrollbar; >4 panes floor at the 25% arm and the row scrolls exactly as today. Pure CSS — **no ResizeObserver on the row** — so window resize reflows live for free.
  - **Gap-adjusted floor** (DD): the literal `max(280px, 25%)` from the backlog would force `4×25% + 3×4px (gap-1) > 100%` → a 12px scrollbar at exactly 4 panes, contradicting the "max 4 visible" intent. `calc(25% - 3px)` (3 gaps × 4px ÷ 4 panes) makes exactly 4 panes fit flush.
  - **Verified** the percentage `min-width` resolves against the flex container's content box (the scrollport), NOT the scrolled content width — the containing block of a flex item is its flex container's content box, and `overflow-x: auto` does not change that. The backlog's JS-measurement fallback is therefore unneeded; the e2e asserts the resulting widths as a safety net.
- **Autofit OFF**: **exactly** the prior per-pane-width behavior — explicit pixel widths from `usePaneWidths.getWidth`, `shrink-0`, resize handles present.
- **Non-destructive round-trip**: the stored `runkit:board-widths:<board>` map is **never touched** by autofit (the `width` prop is merely not passed while on; `getWidth`/`setWidth` are not called through the autofit branch), so toggling OFF restores the exact hand-tuned layout.
- **`autofit?: boolean` prop on `BoardPane`** (not a wrapper div — DD): the pane root is the row's direct flex child AND the `rootRef` IntersectionObserver target (§ Desktop Relay-Connection Suspension), so a wrapper would break both contracts; the flag follows the existing optional-`width` pattern.

**Controls (Constitution V parity)** — a top-bar button and a palette action flip the same state:

- **Top-bar `BoardAutofitToggle`** (`top-bar.tsx`): a **board-only** L2-cluster toggle **between `Aa` (`TerminalFontControl`) and `✕` (`ClosePaneButton`)**, gated `mode === "board" && onToggleAutofit` (unlike Aa/✕ which are terminal+board). Mirrors the `FixedWidthToggle` vocabulary — `aria-pressed={autofit}`, `rk-glint` CRT-glint hover, `coarse:` touch sizing. See § Chrome (Top Bar) → Right cluster (L2).
- **Palette action** `Board: Toggle Autofit (on/off)` (`id: "board-toggle-autofit"`, `boardRouteActions` in `board-page.tsx`, label reflects state) → `toggleAutofit`.
- **State plumbing** — `BoardPage` publishes `autofit` + `onToggleAutofit: toggleAutofit` into the top-bar slot context (`useRegisterTopBarSlot`, the same channel carrying `onCloseFocused`/`closeDisabled`); `top-bar-slot-context.tsx` grows two optional board-mode fields `autofit?` / `onToggleAutofit?`; `RootTopBar` (`app.tsx`) maps `slot?.autofit`/`slot?.onToggleAutofit` → `TopBar` props (tolerant-empty — absent ⇒ no toggle rendered).

**Alignments (no code change)**:

- **`MAX_LIVE_RELAY_PANES = 4`** (§ Desktop Relay-Connection Suspension) equals the 4-visible max the 25% floor produces, so on plaintext origins autofit never forces a visible-but-paused pane; the focused pane is exempt from the cap anyway (`selectLivePanes`). >4 panes still overflow horizontally and off-screen panes still suspend.
- **xterm refit rides the existing `terminal-client.tsx` ResizeObserver** (no autofit-specific wiring): a container `ResizeObserver` rAF-debounces `fitAddon.fit()` + a paired `{type:"resize",cols,rows}` WS message; flex reflow (window resize, pin/unpin, toggle flips) changes each visible pane's size and fires that observer per pane.

**Tests**: unit `use-board-autofit.test.ts` (default-off, "on"-sentinel round-trip + key removal, per-board isolation, board-switch reload, malformed tolerance); Playwright `tests/e2e/board-autofit.spec.ts` + companion `.spec.md` (equal-fill/no-scroll at 2–3 panes, ~25%-floor/scroll at 5+, per-board persistence across reload, handles-hidden-while-on, top-bar button + palette action parity) — run via `just test-e2e`/`just pw` only.

### Board Pane Reorder (`260708-rmiq-board-pane-reorder`)

Desktop board panes are drag-reorderable, with full Cmd+K keyboard parity (Constitution V). Panes render in server `orderKey` order (`GET /api/boards/{name}`); reorder writes a new fractional-index key via the previously-dark `POST /api/boards/{name}/reorder` (see `architecture.md` § Boards Feature — the whole backend half was shipped and unwired before this change). **`MobileCarousel` is untouched** — swipe is navigation there, not reorder.

**Adapts the § Server-tile drag reorder pattern** (`use-server-reorder.ts`) into a sibling hook `useBoardPaneReorder(entries, board, reorder)` (`app/frontend/src/hooks/use-board-pane-reorder.ts`), inheriting its two hard-won fixes (derive-over-store override, self-target dragover acceptance). Key differences from server/session reorder:

- **Custom MIME `application/x-board-pane-reorder`** (`BOARD_PANE_REORDER_MIME`) — must not collide with `application/x-server-reorder`, `application/x-session-reorder`, or the window-move default-JSON payload. Guarded FIRST, before any acceptance (the shared guard-order invariant — see § Server-tile drag reorder).
- **Composite `server:windowId` key** — a board spans servers, so `windowId` alone is ambiguous; the override array, the drag payload, and the DnD/palette bookkeeping all key by `server:windowId` (matching the `key={`${entry.server}:${entry.windowId}`}` in `DesktopRow`).
- **Split handle/drop props** — `getHandleProps(server, windowId)` returns `{ handle, drop }` separately: `handle` (`draggable` + `onDragStart`/`onDragEnd`) goes on the pane HEADER only (`BoardHeader`) so a live xterm terminal never hijacks the drag or becomes the drag image; `drop` (`onDragOver`/`onDrop`) goes on the pane ROOT (`BoardPane`) so the preview updates and a release commits anywhere over a pane, not only the ~24px header strip. The header ✕ unpin button opts out (`draggable={false}` + `stopPropagation`) and the resize handle lives on the pane root outside the header, so neither is shadowed by the drag handle (no regression to unpin or drag-resize).
- **ONE `reorderPin` POST per move, no debounce** — fractional indexing means one authoritative call per completed move (`before`/`after` = the moved pane's new neighbours' windowIds, `null` at edges), so the drop is the single commit point. This is the deliberate contrast with server/session reorder's 250ms debounced full-order writes + drop-flush (there is no full-order sweep to coalesce). The `board-changed` SSE echo (refetched by `useBoardEntries`, 50ms debounce) reconciles the override away.
- **Committed-drop flag drives cancel-revert** — `committedRef` is set true only when `onDrop` fires the POST. `onDragEnd` clears the override when uncommitted (Escape / release outside any pane = revert to authoritative order, no phantom unpersisted order) but keeps it when committed (no snap-back — the SSE echo reconciles it). This is the one place the board hook diverges from the no-drag-end-clear discipline of server/session reorder: with drop as the single commit point, native HTML5 cancel semantics = revert, so the no-snap-back rule applies only to committed drops and SSE reconciles.
- **Rollback on POST rejection** — `usePinActions().reorder` now shows its toast AND **rethrows** (pin/unpin still swallow — they have no client-side optimistic order to revert); the DnD hook `.catch()`es to clear the override and the palette move `.catch()`es to avoid an unhandled rejection, so a rejected reorder reverts the display to the authoritative order instead of leaving the failed order rendered.
- **`onDrop` derives neighbours inline from the final override order** (not from `computeReorderNeighbors` over the authoritative list) — the override is what the user sees and is robust to mid-drag entry churn where index arithmetic over the authoritative array is not. The pure `computeReorderNeighbors`/`computeMoveNeighbors` helpers (`src/lib/board-reorder.ts`, mirroring `palette-move.ts`) are the PALETTE path's arithmetic (`computeReorderNeighbors` has one live caller, `computeMoveNeighbors`, so it is kept with a doc comment, not dead).

**Palette parity** — `Board: Move Focused Pane Left/Right` (`boardRouteActions`, boundary-hidden per § Boards Command Palette) act on the focused pane, compute neighbours via `computeMoveNeighbors`, and fire the same single-POST path as DnD. No wraparound (hidden, not disabled, at the edges).

**Focus tracked by `server:windowId` key + a user-intent gate** (`board-page.tsx`, the load-bearing seam):

- Focus is tracked by the focused pane's **`server:windowId` key** (`focusedKeyRef`), NOT by positional index. A single focus-authority effect reconciles `focusedIndex` from `focusedKeyRef` on every order change (via `focusedIndexForKey`) so the focused pane's identity survives reorders — own palette move, own drop echo, AND a reorder arriving from another client (key-follow, not index-follow). An index bump alone was insufficient: with `paneRefs` keyed to the authoritative order, `setFocusedIndex(i±1)` before the SSE echo routed the imperative xterm `.focus()` into the DISPLACED NEIGHBOUR's terminal (wrong-terminal keystrokes) — so the palette `moveFocusedPane` deliberately does NOT bump `focusedIndex`; the reconcile does it once the new order settles.
- **Imperative `.focus()` fires only on user intent** — this is the board-route form of the "SSE must not steal focus" invariant (the sidebar tree's `focusMovedRef` gate is the sibling — see § Keyboard Navigation & Tree ARIA). `useBoardEntries` refetches a fresh `entries` array on EVERY `board-changed` SSE from ANY board on ANY server, so an unconditional `.focus()` on each identity change would yank DOM focus into the xterm while the user types in the compose buffer / pin-popover / palette / dialogs, and would auto-focus pane 0 on board load. The fix gates `paneRefs.current[focusedIndex]?.focus()` behind `shouldFocusPane(prevFocusedIndexRef.current, focusedIndex)` — it fires only when `focusedIndex` actually changed from the last focused index. The silent key→index reconcile (`setFocusedIndex(j)` early-return) is unchanged, so an own move still lands imperative focus in the moved pane post-echo (the reconcile bumps the index → the re-entered settled pass sees the change → focuses). Board load does not auto-focus pane 0 (index 0 unchanged from its seed). `shouldFocusPane`/`focusedIndexForKey` are unit-tested in `board-reorder.test.ts`.
- **Known residual (should-fix, not shipped)**: the index-change gate cannot distinguish an own-move follow from a REMOTE-driven index reconcile. A `board-changed` from another client/tab that shifts the focused pane's index on THIS board (a remote reorder crossing the focused position, or a remote unpin of an earlier pane) reconciles `focusedIndex` and the settled pass then fires `.focus()`, yanking DOM focus into the xterm. The dominant steal vectors (any-board refetch, same-order refetch, board load) are closed and unit-tested, and amended R6 itself endorses the index-change gate, so this narrow multi-client subcase was graded should-fix and deferred. A true intent flag (mirror the sidebar's `focusMovedRef` — set on `moveFocusedPane`/click/cycle/own drop; the reconcile branch would advance `prevFocusedIndexRef` when no intent is pending) would close it.

**e2e** (`app/frontend/tests/e2e/board-reorder.spec.ts` + `.spec.md`) mirrors `server-reorder.spec.ts`: it exercises the reorder ENDPOINT + `board-changed` SSE echo + a reload-free GET-order assertion against the live backend, NOT a native HTML5 drag simulation — synthetic Playwright DnD is unreliable (the session-reorder drag spec is `test.fixme`, never passed) and `page.reload()` does not commit under the SPA's long-lived SSE. The drag handlers, MIME guard, reconcile, cancel-revert, failure-rollback, and neighbour arithmetic are Vitest-covered (`use-board-pane-reorder.test.ts`, `board-reorder.test.ts`). Backend cross-server neighbour resolution is Go-tested (`router_test.go` `TestLookupNeighbourKeys_*`).

### Desktop Relay-Connection Suspension

On plaintext origins, `DesktopRow` suspends off-screen panes' relay WebSockets so the live-connection count stays under the browser's HTTP/1.1 ~6-per-origin cap — the desktop analogue of the mobile carousel's `paused={idx !== carouselIndex}` pause. Added by `260531-rus8-bound-desktop-relay-websockets`. The mechanism mirrors the proven mobile pause: a paused pane unmounts its `TerminalClient`, which closes the `/relay/<wid>` WebSocket (the `cancelled` flag blocks the reconnect, so the slot genuinely frees); scroll-back re-mounts and re-opens, replaying terminal content.

- **Plaintext-only gate** — the entire feature is gated on `plaintext = window.location.protocol === "http:"` (`board-page.tsx`). On HTTPS/h2 (production via Tailscale) every desktop pane stays live (`paused={false}`), no `IntersectionObserver` is created, and no cap applies — behavior is byte-identical to before this change. The ~6-connection ceiling is a plaintext HTTP/1.1 artifact (h2 multiplexes; the relay WS limit is ~255), so the fix activates only where the problem exists (E2E/dev `http://localhost:3020`, raw-port `http://...` access)
- **Visibility via `IntersectionObserver`** — on plaintext origins, a single observer rooted on the `rowRef` horizontal-scroll container drives each pane's `paused` prop from viewport intersection. Panes are keyed to indices via a `data-paneIndex` attribute on each pane's root element (forwarded through a `rootRef` callback prop on `BoardPane`, kept distinct from the `paneRefs` imperative `BoardPaneHandle` so neither contract leaks into the other). The observer effect mirrors the existing wheel-handler effect's setup/cleanup discipline (`observer.disconnect()` on unmount) and re-subscribes when the pane count changes
- **Pre-warm margin** — the observer uses `RELAY_PREWARM_ROOT_MARGIN` = `` `0px ${BOARD_PANE_DEFAULT_WIDTH}px` `` (one pane-width of horizontal `rootMargin`, vertical 0) so a pane is kept live slightly before it enters and after it leaves the strict viewport, preventing pause/resume thrash (and the `[reconnecting...]` flicker) on a quick scroll-past. No debounce in v1 — add one only if thrash is observed during Playwright tuning
- **Live-pane cap** — simultaneously-live (unpaused) relay panes are capped at `MAX_LIVE_RELAY_PANES = 4` (named constant, not a magic number), backstopping the observer for the wide-monitor case where more panes fit on-screen than the budget allows (`1 SSE + 4 relay + headroom` stays under 6). When visibility alone would leave more than the cap live, the **least-recently-focused** visible panes are paused first. The selection logic is the pure `selectLivePanes` helper in `app/frontend/src/components/board/select-live-panes.ts` (colocated unit tests), consuming the visible-index set, the focused index, the most-recently-focused order, and the cap; `DesktopRow` passes `paused={!livePanes.has(idx)}` (and short-circuits to `paused={false}` when `livePanes === null`, i.e. on secure origins). The MRU order folds the current `focusedIndex` to the front during render (`useMemo` keyed on `focusedIndex`) so cap eviction never sees a stale focus
- **Focused pane always live** — `selectLivePanes` adds `focusedIndex` unconditionally before filling the remaining slots, so the focused pane is exempt from both visibility-pause and the cap. This preserves `Cmd+]`/`Cmd+[` cycling (cycling to an off-screen paused pane re-selects it → unpauses → re-mounts → imperative `focus()` via `paneRefs`) and BottomBar targeting of the focused terminal
- **Composes with the sibling change** — `260531-m3pl-static-xterm-imports` removes the xterm chunk-fetch pressure from the runtime connection budget while this change bounds the persistent relay streams; together they fit the board route under the 6-connection cap on plaintext origins (the original board-route E2E hang root cause). `MobileCarousel` is untouched — it already suspended correctly

### Mobile Single-Pane Carousel

Below the `min-width: 640px` breakpoint (matching the existing project mobile convention), the BoardPage renders a single-pane swipe carousel:

- One pane fills the viewport width
- Touch swipe left/right cycles in `orderKey` order; threshold 40px on `touchstart` → `touchend` `clientX` delta
- **Off-screen panes pause** by unmounting their `TerminalClient` so the WebSocket closes; on swipe-in, the pane re-mounts and the terminal reattaches
- A pagination dot strip indicates the current pane index (no wrap on edges in v1)

### Sidebar Boards Section (`app/frontend/src/components/sidebar/boards-section.tsx`)

Renders **at the very top of the sidebar** — the section order is **Boards → Servers → Sessions** (`260509-17m3-rotated-shell-layout` reordered this from the previous Servers → Boards → Sessions). Visible on every route that mounts `<Sidebar>` (`/$server/...` and `/board/$name`). The board route reuses the same `BoardsSection` component for board switching; there is no separate BoardPage listing.

- **Always visible**, regardless of `boards.length` or current route
- **Hint mode** — when `boards.length === 0`, the body shows a one-line hint `Pin a window to start a board` (`text-xs text-text-secondary`) verbatim from 4vuv's copy. Applies on every route, not only on `/board/<name>` — placing Boards at the top would cause a layout shift if the section hid/showed dynamically (Servers would jump up, then back down when the first board materializes)
- **First board materializes** — hint replaced by a single board row in place; no other section's vertical position shifts
- **Last board removed** — section reverts to hint mode; no layout shift to ServerPanel or Sessions

Each row: board name (left, truncate with ellipsis), pin count (right, muted), highlighted background when current route matches `/board/<name>`. Clicking the row navigates to `/board/<name>`. **Drag-reorderable** (`260708-a2qd-board-list-reorder`): rows render `orderedBoards` from the shared `useBoardListReorder` hook with `getTileProps(b.name)` spread onto each, and the dragged row dims via `opacity-50` — see § Board-list drag reorder.

### Sidebar Pin Icon on Window Rows

`window-row.tsx` gains a pin icon button that follows the existing icon-on-hover pattern in the sidebar:

- **Hover-revealed** (always visible on touch devices via `coarse:opacity-100`)
- **Filled** when the window is pinned to ANY board; **outline** when not pinned (computed via `useWindowPins(server, windowId)` which watches every board)
- **Click opens `PinPopover`** (`app/frontend/src/components/sidebar/pin-popover.tsx`) anchored to the icon: list of existing boards (each row pins or unpins on click), plus an inline "Pin to new board…" text input (Enter validates against the board-name regex and creates the board on first pin). Validation errors surface inline. Outside-click + Escape dismiss

### Active-Board Highlight in Sessions Tree

When the current route is `/board/<name>`, `WindowRow` applies an accent left-border to windows pinned to **that specific board only**. Pins to other boards do NOT trigger the highlight. The pin icon's filled state is independent (always reflects "pinned to ANY board"). On non-board routes, no highlight is applied.

### Pin Entry Points

| Entry point | Location | Notes |
|-------------|----------|-------|
| Sidebar pin icon | `WindowRow` (every server's window rows in the unified sidebar — server routes and board routes alike) | Hover-revealed; popover with board picker + inline input |
| Command palette | `boardActions` block in `app.tsx` (AppShell mount) and BoardPage's own mount | See § Boards Command Palette |
| Board pane header | `BoardHeader` (only on `/board/<name>`) | Per-pane unpin button — no confirmation (pin is cheap to restore) |

Right-click context menu was deliberately NOT implemented in v1 — there is no existing context-menu pattern in the sidebar to extend, and the three entry points above cover all flows.

### Boards Command Palette (`Board:` prefix)

`boardActions: PaletteAction[]` is composed in a dedicated `useMemo` block in `app.tsx`, between `windowActions` and `viewActions`:

```ts
const paletteActions = useMemo(
  () => [...sessionActions, ...windowActions, ...boardActions, ...viewActions, ...terminalFontActions, ...themeActions, ...configActions, ...updateActions, ...serverActions, ...pushActions, ...windowSwitchActions, ...agentActions],
  [...]
);
```

(`pushActions` is the Web Push opt-in block — see § Notifications (Web Push opt-in); `updateActions` is the `run-kit: Update…` block — see § Update Notification, folded in after `configActions` and before `serverActions`, followed by `maintenanceActions` then `versionActions` (`260715-ifco` `run-kit: Version — v…` — see § Steady-state version surfaces) still before `serverActions`; `windowSwitchActions`/`agentActions` still compose last.)

| Entry | Visibility | Action |
|-------|------------|--------|
| `Board: Switch to <name>` (one per board, `(current)` on the active one) | Always | Navigate to `/board/<name>` |
| `Board: Pin Current Window` | Only on `/$server/$window` | Dispatches `pin-popover:open` to the matching `WindowRow` |
| `Board: Unpin Current Window` | Only when current window is pinned to ≥1 board | Unpins from all boards the current window is pinned to (single-action — no per-board picker in v1) |
| `Board: Leave Board View` | Only on `/board/<name>` | Navigate to last viewed window route, or `/` if none |
| `Board: Cycle Pane Focus →` | Only on `/board/<name>` and ≥1 pane | Same as `Cmd+]` |
| `Board: Cycle Pane Focus ←` | Only on `/board/<name>` and ≥1 pane | Same as `Cmd+[` |
| `Board: Unpin Focused Pane` (`260704-9o7k`) | Only on `/board/<name>` and ≥1 pane | Unpins the focused entry (`entries[focusedIndex]`) — keyboard parity for the top-bar board ✕ (Constitution V); non-destructive, NOT a kill |
| `Board: Move up` / `Board: Move down` (`260708-a2qd`) | Only on `/board/<name>`, boundary-hidden (not first / not last) | Reorder the CURRENT board in the board list — keyboard/touch parity for the board-list drag (Constitution V). Computes the full order via `computeMoveOrder` and POSTs `setBoardOrder`; see § Board-list drag reorder + § Command Palette Move up/down |
| `Board: Move Focused Pane Left` (`260708-rmiq`) | Only on `/board/<name>` when `focusedIndex > 0` (hidden at the left edge — not disabled) | Moves the focused pane one slot left — fires the same single `reorder(...)` POST as DnD, computing `before`/`after` via `computeMoveNeighbors` (§ Board Pane Reorder). No wraparound. Keyboard parity for the drag reorder (Constitution V) |
| `Board: Move Focused Pane Right` (`260708-rmiq`) | Only on `/board/<name>` when `focusedIndex < entries.length - 1` (hidden at the right edge) | Moves the focused pane one slot right — mirror of Move Left |
| `Board: Toggle Autofit (on/off)` (`260708-738w`, `id: board-toggle-autofit`) | Only on `/board/<name>` (label reflects the current state) | Flips the per-board desktop autofit preference (same state the top-bar `BoardAutofitToggle` reflects — Constitution V parity). Desktop layout only; a no-op on the mobile carousel. See § Board Autofit Toggle |

**v1 limits**: The right-click context menu pin entry is not implemented (use sidebar pin icon, command palette, or board pane header). Hover-to-focus is disabled in v1. *(The former "`Board: Reorder Pane` deferred to v1.1" limit is superseded by `260708-rmiq` — DnD reorder + the Move Focused Pane Left/Right palette entries above ship the reorder capability. See § Board Pane Reorder.)*

The AppShell palette mount carries `Switch to <name>` + `Pin Current Window` + `Unpin Current Window`. The BoardPage's own palette mount (`boardRouteActions` useMemo in `board-page.tsx`) carries `Switch to <name>` + `Leave Board View` + the boundary-hidden `Board: Move up/down` (`260708-a2qd`) + the entries-gated `Cycle Pane Focus →/←` + `Unpin Focused Pane` (`260704-9o7k`) + the boundary-gated `Move Focused Pane Left/Right` (`260708-rmiq`; Left pushed only when `focusedIndex > 0`, Right only when `focusedIndex < entries.length - 1`; the cycle/unpin/move-pane entries all sit inside a single `entries.length > 0` guard) + the always-present `Board: Toggle Autofit (on/off)` (`260708-738w`, § Board Autofit Toggle — parity for the top-bar `BoardAutofitToggle`, outside the `entries.length > 0` guard) — board-route-only entries that AppShell's palette can't surface because the board route does not render AppShell — **plus** the globally-meaningful actions duplicated in because the board mounts its own palette: the terminal-font trio (Increase / Decrease / Reset terminal font — the board's panes are live terminals, § Terminal Font Size) followed by `View: Refresh Page` and `Help: Documentation`. The returned array composes as `[...switchEntries, ...conditional, ...fontEntries, refreshEntry, helpEntry]` (`refreshEntry` from `260703-p29w`, `helpEntry` from `260704-hmd0`). The board is the degraded-relay recovery scenario — N live relay WebSockets — and since `260704-9o7k` a top-bar RefreshButton also renders in board mode (L3 always-block), so the palette entry is now the keyboard-parity form rather than the board's *only* reload affordance. **Since `260713-4zap`** the return array also appends `...updateEntries` (`buildUpdateActions`, § Update Notification) LAST — `[...switchEntries, ...conditional, ...fontEntries, refreshEntry, helpEntry, ...updateEntries]` — following the same dual-mount duplication convention: below `sm` the top-bar UpdateChip is hidden, so the board palette is a phone user's only update surface on `/board/$name`.

### Command Palette View actions (`View:` prefix)

`viewActions: PaletteAction[]` (`useMemo` in `app.tsx`) is the AppShell palette's `View:`-prefixed block, composed into `paletteActions` between `boardActions` and `terminalFontActions` (see § Boards Command Palette). Its static entries are:

| Entry | Visibility | Action |
|-------|------------|--------|
| `View: Text Input` | Only when `sessionName` is set (a terminal is in view) | Opens the compose buffer (`setComposeOpen(true)`) |
| `View: Terminal` / `View: Web` / `View: Chat` (`260714-t97o-web-view-lens`; chat `260714-r7rq`) | Each shown only when its lens is **available** (`availableViews(currentWindow)`, which folds in the `chatProvider` gate) **AND not the current** (`resolvedView`) view; `shortcut` hint = `` Ctrl+` `` for `View: Chat` (and `View: Terminal` when LEAVING chat), else `⌘.` | `switchView(view)` — the per-viewer lens switch (no `@rk_type` mutation). Built by the ONE pure `buildViewActions(available, resolved, onSwitch)` (`lib/palette-view.ts`); see § Window Views (Lens Model) → Palette parity. **Replaced the retired `toggle-iframe-terminal`** action (which mutated `@rk_type`) AND the chat feature's separate `buildViewActions(chatAvailable, …)` call |
| `View: Fixed Width (900px)` / `View: Full Width` | Always (label reflects `fixedWidth` state) | `toggleFixedWidth` |
| `View: Refresh Page` | Always (ungated) | `window.location.reload()` — a full page reload (`260703-p29w-topbar-refresh-button`) |

**`refresh-page` is appended ungated after `toggle-fixed-width`** — a full-page reload is meaningful on every AppShell route (Server Cabin `/$server`, Terminal `/$server/$window`), unlike the terminal-only top-bar `RefreshButton` (§ Chrome (Top Bar)). It is the keyboard-reachable form of that recovery affordance (constitution V).

**Dual-mount duplication** — because the app mounts **two** CommandPalettes (AppShell's, driven by `paletteActions`; and the board route's own, driven by `boardRouteActions`) and the board route does NOT render AppShell, a globally-meaningful action must be **registered in both** to be reachable everywhere. `refresh-page` follows the **terminal-font-trio precedent** (Increase/Decrease/Reset terminal font, § Terminal Font Size): both the trio and `refresh-page` live in `app.tsx`'s AppShell blocks AND are duplicated into `board-page.tsx`'s `boardRouteActions` (§ Boards Command Palette). This is intentional duplication, not a shared source — the two palettes have disjoint mounts. The `run-kit: Update…`/`Dismiss Update Notice` actions (`260713-4zap`, § Update Notification) follow the SAME convention — built by the shared pure `buildUpdateActions` helper (`lib/palette-update.ts`) and folded into BOTH `app.tsx`'s `updateActions` and `board-page.tsx`'s `boardRouteActions` — with the extra motivation that below `sm` the top-bar UpdateChip is hidden, so the board palette is a phone user's only update surface. The **Cockpit (`/`) mounts NO CommandPalette** (pre-existing — the Cockpit `ServerListPage` has no palette), so `refresh-page` is unreachable there and that was scoped out (adding a Cockpit palette mount would grow UI surface against constitution §IV). Nothing in the codebase claims broader reach than "every mounted palette" — the reach comments at `app.tsx` `viewActions` and the `top-bar.tsx` `RefreshButton` docblock name the actual scope (AppShell palette + board palette; Cockpit mounts none).

### Hooks (Frontend)

| Hook | File | Returns |
|------|------|---------|
| `useBoards()` | `hooks/use-boards.ts` | `{ boards, isLoading, error }`. Initial `listBoards()` on mount; subscribes to `board-changed` SSE on every server returned by `listServers()` (boards are server-scoped since `260602-qn62`, but the board LIST is summarized across servers, so it attaches all to catch each one's pin/unpin/reorder events); 50ms debounce coalesces rapid events; preserves last good value on transient error |
| `useBoardEntries(name)` | `hooks/use-boards.ts` | `{ entries, isLoading, error }`. Initial `getBoard(name)`; subscribes on all known servers (the board list spans servers, so a pin/unpin on any server may affect this board); same debounce + error tolerance |
| `usePinActions(board?)` | `hooks/use-pin-actions.ts` | `{ pin, unpin, reorder }` stable callbacks; toast on error; optimistic — SSE re-broadcast reconciles |
| `usePaneWidths(boardName, sidebarWidth)` | `hooks/use-pane-widths.ts` | `{ getWidth, setWidth }`; reads/writes `localStorage["runkit:board-widths:<name>"]`; clamps to `[280, viewport - sidebar]`; default 480px |
| `useBoardAutofit(board)` (`260708-738w`) | `hooks/use-board-autofit.ts` | `{ autofit, toggleAutofit }`; per-board desktop autofit preference in `localStorage["runkit:board-autofit:<board>"]` ("on" sentinel; OFF removes the key); default off; reloads on `board` change (mirrors `usePaneWidths`). Never touches `runkit:board-widths:<board>`. See § Board Autofit Toggle |
| `useIsMobile()` | `hooks/use-is-mobile.ts` | `boolean`; `matchMedia("(max-width: 640px)")` listener |
| `useActiveBoardName()` | `hooks/use-active-board.ts` | active board name from `/board/<name>` route, else `null` |
| `useWindowPins(server, windowId)` | `hooks/use-window-pins.ts` | list of boards the window is pinned to; drives the pin-icon filled state |
| `useNow()` | `hooks/use-now.ts` | current epoch seconds (`Math.floor(Date.now()/1000)`); self-ticks every 1s via `setInterval` (cleared on unmount), re-rendering ONLY the calling leaf. Display-only clock — NOT data polling. Scope to duration leaves so the tick never re-renders ancestors; see § Render Performance (`260613-ect6`) |
| `useUpdateNotification()` (`260713-4zap`) | `contexts/session-context.tsx` (exported alongside the provider) | `{ qualifies, showChip, latest, current, updateNow, dismissUpdate, daemonVersion, brew, forceUpdateNow, restartNow }` — the DERIVED update-notification display shape read by the top-bar `UpdateChip` + the palette `buildUpdateActions`/`buildMaintenanceActions` callers (and the connection-dot title). Reads `SessionContext` via `useContext` DIRECTLY (provider-tolerant — never throws outside the provider; each field falls back). `qualifies = !isDev && latest !== null`; `showChip = qualifies && latest !== updateDismissedVersion`; `current = updateAvailable?.current ?? null` (`260715-ifco` — the UpdateChip transition title). Self-contained-consumer pattern (mirrors `usePushSubscription`). See § Update Notification |

## Notifications (Web Push opt-in)

`260615-xd9r-web-push-notifications` adds browser Web Push so `rk notify` (and any process on the box) can deliver an OS notification that reaches the user **even when the RunKit PWA tab is closed**. The end-to-end backend/delivery model lives in `architecture.md` § Web Push Notifications; this section covers the frontend opt-in surface.

**The opt-in is a Cmd+K palette entry — NOT a bell.** Per Constitution §V (Keyboard-First) and §IV (Minimal Surface Area, no new route/settings page), the entire opt-in gesture is a single command-palette action. The label reflects subscription state and is **terminal-themed text**, never a bell icon (an explicit user decision — a bell was rejected):

| Palette label | When | Action |
|---------------|------|--------|
| `Notifications: Enable push` | Not yet subscribed | Runs the enable flow: `Notification.requestPermission()` → on `granted`, `getVapidPublicKey()` (`GET /api/push/vapid-public-key`) → `registration.pushManager.subscribe({userVisibleOnly: true, applicationServerKey})` → `subscribePush(sub)` (`POST /api/push/subscribe`) |
| `Notifications: Enabled ✓` | Already subscribed | Reflects state; the `✓` is a Unicode checkmark (terminal-themed glyph, not a bell) |

**Wiring**: `usePushSubscription()` (`app/frontend/src/hooks/use-push-subscription.ts`) returns `{ state, actions }` where `actions` is the `pushActions: PaletteAction[]` block; it is threaded into `app.tsx`'s `paletteActions` useMemo (spread just before `windowSwitchActions` — see § Boards Command Palette for the composition). The flow logic is the self-contained `app/frontend/src/lib/push.ts` module (`registerServiceWorker()`, `enablePushSubscription()`, `getPushState()`) plus the `getVapidPublicKey()`/`subscribePush()` client functions in `api/client.ts` — a separate module rather than inlining into the 1600-line, SSE-coupled `app.tsx`. The service worker (`public/sw.js`) is registered on app load from `main.tsx`.

**Fail-silent / secure-context**: every path is throw-free. `registerServiceWorker()` is guarded by `'serviceWorker' in navigator` and no-ops on unsupported / insecure-context environments. The enable flow aborts silently (a toast is acceptable) when permission is denied or push is unsupported / the context is insecure, sending no subscription. Web Push (service worker + `PushManager`) requires a **secure context — HTTPS or `localhost`**; the user typically hits run-kit on `localhost:3000` or behind a TLS proxy (both secure), but raw-IP plaintext access simply cannot subscribe (silently).

## Update Notification (`260713-4zap-update-notify-one-click-upgrade`)

Notifies the web-UI user when a newer minor/major run-kit release is available and offers a one-click upgrade that brew-upgrades the daemon and restarts it. **In-app ONLY — explicitly NO Web Push** (user-decided: Web Push is reserved for waiting agents; update notices must not buzz phones). Two surfaces — a top-bar L3 chip + command-palette actions — both self-contained consumers of one context hook, mirroring the `NotificationControl`/`usePushSubscription` precedent (no props threaded through `RootTopBar`→`TopBar`). The backend origin (SSE `event: version`/`event: update-available`, `POST /api/update`, `internal/updatecheck`) is in [architecture.md](/run-kit/architecture.md) § SSE Hub / § API Layer; this section is the frontend surface.

### Context state + `useUpdateNotification()` hook

`SessionContext` (`contexts/session-context.tsx`) owns the update state (it already owns the server-global SSE pool + `?metrics=1` stream, and `version`/`update-available` are server-global like `server-order`/`board-order`, so this reuses the exact fan-out — no second context). It exposes:

- `daemonVersion: string | null` — the running daemon version from `event: version` (no leading `v`), `null` until first seen.
- `updateAvailable: { current, latest } | null` — the pending qualifying update from `event: update-available`, `null` when none.
- `updateDismissedVersion: string | null` — the per-version dismissal from localStorage `runkit-update-dismissed` (const `UPDATE_DISMISSED_KEY`), lazily read in a try/catch on mount.
- `updateNow(): Promise<void>` — thin wrapper over the `triggerUpdate()` client helper (`POST /api/update`; rejects on non-2xx).
- `dismissUpdate(): void` — writes the current `updateAvailable.latest` to localStorage `runkit-update-dismissed` + sets `updateDismissedVersion`.
- **`brew: boolean`** (since `260714-3law-force-update-restart-palette`) — whether the daemon is a Homebrew install, from the `event: version` `brew` field. Tracked in React `useState` (`isBrew`, drives palette visibility → must re-render, unlike the reload-decision refs below), **default `false` until the first version event is observed** (so the brew-gated `run-kit: Update Now` palette entry stays hidden on the brief pre-connect window; mirrors the existing `qualifies` absent-data-hidden gating). Set inside `applyVersion`.
- **`forceUpdateNow(): Promise<void>`** (since `260714-3law`) — thin wrapper over `triggerForceUpdate()` (`POST /api/update` body `{"force":true}`; rejects on non-2xx). Same shape as `updateNow`.
- **`restartNow(): Promise<void>`** (since `260714-3law`) — thin wrapper over `triggerRestart()` (`POST /api/restart`; rejects on non-2xx).

The `version`/`update-available` listeners are added on **BOTH** stream kinds — the per-server pool `EventSource` AND the dedicated `?metrics=1` `EventSource` — server-global, applied idempotently (no `data.server` filter), exactly like `server-order`/`board-order`. Both call the pure-ish `applyVersion` / `applyUpdateAvailable` callbacks; malformed events are skipped. **`applyVersion(version, boot, brew)`** (since `260714-3law`, signature extended from `applyVersion(version)`) parses the payload as `{ version?, boot?, brew? }` **tolerantly** on both listeners — `boot` is passed only when `typeof data.boot === "string"` (else `null`), `brew` as `data.brew === true` (defaults `false`) — so an older daemon's boot-less/brew-less payload (a mixed-version window) never breaks parsing or flips brew true.

**Tolerant `useUpdateNotification()` hook** (exported from `session-context.tsx`) — reads the context via `useContext(SessionContext)` DIRECTLY (not `useSessionContext`, so it **never throws outside the provider**; every field falls back — `updateNow`/`forceUpdateNow`/`restartNow` → `() => Promise.resolve()`, `dismissUpdate` → `() => {}`, `brew` → `false`). It returns the DERIVED display shape the chip + palette consume, so the gating logic lives in one place:

- `isDev = daemonVersion === DEV_VERSION` (`"dev"`).
- `latest = updateAvailable?.latest ?? null`.
- **`qualifies = !isDev && latest !== null`** — the frontend trusts the server's `update-available` event for the semver qualification (the backend already applied the minor/major-only rule); it only additionally suppresses the `dev` daemon and requires a pending latest. It does NOT re-run a semver compare.
- **`showChip = qualifies && latest !== updateDismissedVersion`** — the chip's per-version dismissal gate. A later release with a different `latest` re-shows the chip (the dismissal key is per-version), because a newer qualifying release re-broadcasts `update-available` (the backend checker's re-fire gate) → `updateDismissedVersion` no longer equals `latest`.
- **`current = updateAvailable?.current ?? null`** (since `260715-ifco-expose-running-version-ui`) — the version the daemon is currently ON per the pending `update-available` event, exposed so the `UpdateChip` can render the `v{current} → v{latest}` transition instead of only the target. `null` when no update is pending (the chip falls back to target-only wording). Distinct from `daemonVersion` (the always-present running version from `event: version`): `current` rides the `update-available` payload and so is present exactly when the chip is.
- Returns `{ qualifies, showChip, latest, current, updateNow, dismissUpdate, daemonVersion, brew, forceUpdateNow, restartNow }` (`brew`/`daemonVersion`/`forceUpdateNow`/`restartNow` added by `260714-3law` so the maintenance palette entries can gate on `brew`/`daemonVersion` and fire the two actions — see § Maintenance palette entries below; `current` added by `260715-ifco` for the UpdateChip transition title — see § Steady-state version surfaces below). `daemonVersion` is surfaced raw because `buildMaintenanceActions` does its own `version === "dev"` gate.

### Reload guard — `shouldReloadOnVersion` (post-restart auto-reload, boot-aware since `260714-3law`)

After a one-click upgrade the daemon restarts, which drops SSE; the reconnect delivers a **different** `event: version`, and the open tab is now stale (it embeds the old frontend assets baked into the old binary). The guard auto-reloads it exactly once. **Since `260714-3law-force-update-restart-palette` the guard also fires on a same-version restart** (a plain `POST /api/restart`, a config-change/wedge-recovery restart, or a restart initiated from SSH) via the per-process `boot` id — so a tab that reconnects to a **new process at the same version** is no longer left silently running stale in-memory state:

- The pure exported predicate is now **4-arg**: `shouldReloadOnVersion(firstVersion: string | null, firstBoot: string | null, nextVersion: string, nextBoot: string | null): boolean` (widened from the pre-`3law` 2-arg `shouldReloadOnVersion(firstSeen, next)`). Logic, in order: (1) `firstVersion === null` → `false` (**never reload on first connect** — no reload loop, the invariant `4zap` established, unchanged); (2) `nextVersion !== firstVersion` → `true` (a version change means new assets — the original reload trigger); (3) **same version** → reload on a **boot change** UNLESS the version is `"dev"`: `nextVersion === DEV_VERSION` returns `false` (the **air-recompile storm guard** — under `just dev`, air recompiles the backend on every save, minting a fresh boot id each time; reloading every dev tab on every recompile would be a reload storm; a dev version never changes so version-based reload is moot in practice, but the guard keeps the predicate honest), else `nextBoot !== null && nextBoot !== firstBoot`. A **null `nextBoot`** (older daemon, mixed-version window) never triggers the boot branch.
- `applyVersion(version, boot, brew)` (the `version`-listener callback): sets `daemonVersion` + `isBrew`; if `shouldReloadOnVersion(firstVersionRef.current, firstBootRef.current, version, boot)` → `location.reload()` (and returns); else, **only on the first-ever version** (`firstVersionRef.current === null`), stamps BOTH `firstVersionRef.current = version` and `firstBootRef.current = boot`. Both `firstVersionRef` and `firstBootRef` (new in `3law`) are `useRef` (not state — the reload decision must not re-render) so `applyVersion` stays referentially stable.
- Coverage this buys: update (version change), plain restart (boot change, same version), every open tab (the version slot is replayed per SSE connect), and restarts initiated from SSH or crash-recovery (the signal is server-originated, not client-action-originated).

### Top-bar L3 UpdateChip (`UpdateChip` in `top-bar.tsx`)

A self-contained chip in the always-visible L3 right cluster, **leading `NotificationControl`** (the L3 order is Update → Notification → Theme → Refresh → Help → connection dot). Reads `useUpdateNotification()`; wrapped in the cluster's `hidden sm:flex` span (so it is hidden below `sm` — which is why the palette carries the update surface for phone users, see below).

- **Hide gate**: `if (!showChip || !latest) return null` — the three intake hide conditions (no qualifying update / dismissed-for-latest / daemon is `dev`) are all folded into `showChip` inside the hook (dev via `qualifies`, dismissal via `latest !== updateDismissedVersion`, no-update via `latest === null`).
- **Rest state**: an accent chip `⬆ v{latest}` — `border-accent-green text-accent-green` + `rk-glint` CRT-glint hover (the button hover vocabulary, § Hover-Animation Vocabulary). The `⬆` and label are JS string expressions (`{`⬆ v${latest}`}`), rendering a real up-arrow. **`title`/`aria-label`** show the `v{current} → v{latest}` transition (since `260715-ifco`): a computed `restLabel = current ? `Update run-kit: v${current} → v${latest}` : `Update run-kit to v${latest}`` — the target-only wording is retained as the null-`current` fallback (never dead code; `current` is present whenever the chip renders — see § Steady-state version surfaces). The visible chip TEXT is unchanged (`⬆ v{latest}`); only the hover title/aria carry the transition.
- **Click → one-click trigger**: `handleUpdate` early-returns if already `updating`, sets local `updating` state, then `void updateNow().catch(...)`. On the happy path the daemon restart reloads the tab, so `updating` is never cleared; on failure it clears `updating` and shows an error toast (`addToast(msg, "error")`). The busy state renders a `<LogoSpinner size={12}>` + `<span>{"updating…"}</span>` — **the busy label is a JS string expression `{"updating…"}`** (a real `…` U+2026), NOT raw JSX text; JSX text does NOT process JS escape sequences, so a raw `…` in text would render the six literal characters (the cycle-2 must-fix that shipped this form; `update-chip.test.tsx` asserts the exact visible text `updating…`).
- **Dismiss `✕`**: a small sibling button (rendered only when `!updating`, `aria-label="Dismiss update notice"`, label `{"✕"}`) → `dismissUpdate()` (per-version localStorage). Dismissal silences only the chip; the palette action remains (keyboard-first recoverability, §V).

### Palette parity — `run-kit:` actions via `buildUpdateActions` (`lib/palette-update.ts`)
